import torch
import torch.nn as nn


class Model(nn.Module):
    """
    Forward algorithm for Hidden Markov Models.  Computes the log-
    likelihood log p(observations) by iterating the forward recursion
    in log-space for numerical stability.  The dominant inner loop in
    HMM training (Baum-Welch) and Viterbi decoding.
    """

    def __init__(self, num_states, num_obs):
        super().__init__()
        self.num_states = num_states
        self.num_obs = num_obs

        self.log_init = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states))
        self.log_trans = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_states))
        self.log_emit = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_obs))

    def _normalize_log(self, x, dim=-1):
        return x - torch.logsumexp(x, dim=dim, keepdim=True)

    def forward(self, observations: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Args:
            observations: (B, T) – integer observation indices (as long tensor)
        Returns:
            log_lik: (B,) – log p(observations) under the HMM
        """
        B, T = observations.shape
        log_pi = self._normalize_log(self.log_init)
        log_A = self._normalize_log(self.log_trans, dim=-1)
        log_B = self._normalize_log(self.log_emit, dim=-1)

        # Initial step
        emit_0 = log_B[:, observations[:, 0]].t()  # (B, S)
        log_alpha = log_pi.unsqueeze(0) + emit_0

        for t in range(1, T):
            # Transition: log_alpha[b, j] = logsumexp_i(log_alpha[b, i] + log_A[i, j])
            log_alpha = log_alpha.unsqueeze(-1) + log_A.unsqueeze(0)  # (B, S, S)
            log_alpha = torch.logsumexp(log_alpha, dim=1)  # (B, S)
            emit_t = log_B[:, observations[:, t]].t()
            log_alpha = log_alpha + emit_t

        log_lik = torch.logsumexp(log_alpha, dim=-1)
        return log_lik


num_states = 16
num_obs = 64
seq_len = 128
batch_size = 64


def get_inputs():
    return [torch.randint(0, num_obs, (batch_size, seq_len))]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [num_states, num_obs]

This problem is asking me to write a custom CUDA kernel for the forward algorithm of Hidden Markov Models (HMM). Let me understand the computation first. The reference model does: 1. Normalize log_init, log_trans, log_emit 2. For each batch and time step: - Initial step: log_alpha = log_init + log_emit[:, obs[:,0]].T - For t=1 to T-1: log_alpha = log_alpha.unsqueeze(-1) + log_A.unsqueeze(0) // (B, S, S) log_alpha = torch.logsumexp(log_alpha, dim=1) // (B, S) emit_t = log_B[:, observations[:, t]].t() log_alpha = log_alpha + emit_t - Finally: log_lik = torch.logsumexp(log_alpha, dim=-1) Key observations: - num_states = 16 (small and constant-ish) - num_obs = 64 - seq_len = 128 - batch_size = 64 - This is a sequence of matrix-vector operations in log-space Since num_states = 16 is very small, I can use shared memory and cooperative loading. The core operation per time step is: 1. log_alpha_new[b, j] = logsumexp_i(log_alpha[b, i] + log_A[i, j]) 2. log_alpha_new[b, j] = log_alpha_new[b, j] + log_B[j, obs[b, t]] This is essentially a matrix-vector product in log-space followed by broadcasted addition. In normal space: alpha_new[b, :] = alpha[b, :] @ A, then multiply by emit. In log-space: log_alpha_new[b, j] = logsumexp_i(log_alpha[b, i] + log_A[i, j]) For S=16, this is very small. The naive approach is: - For each batch element b and state j, compute over i=0..15: log_alpha[b, i] + log_A[i, j], then take logsumexp. Since S=16 is tiny, we could compute this very efficiently. The main bottleneck is likely memory bandwidth and the logsumexp computation. Since we're iterating over T=128 time steps, and doing B*S*S = 64*16*16 = 16K additions per step, plus B*S logsumexps = 1K per step, total is about 2M ops per time step, 256M ops total. But the PyTorch implementation is probably slow because: 1. It launches many small kernels (one per time step) 2. Each kernel is very small and launch overhead dominates So the key optimization is to fuse the entire T-loop into a single CUDA kernel! For each batch element b, we have a sequence of length T. Let's design the CUDA kernel. ```cuda template <int S> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel( const int* observations, const float* log_init, const float* log_A, const float* log_B, float* output, int B, int T, int num_obs) { // Each block handles NSEQ sequences // Thread mapping: state = threadIdx.x % S, seq = threadIdx.x / S const int seq = blockIdx.x * NSEQ_PER_BLOCK + threadIdx.x / S; const int j = threadIdx.x % S; if (seq >= B) return; __shared__ float s_log_A[S * S]; __shared__ float s_log_alpha[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK][S]; __shared__ int s_obs[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK]; // Load log_A cooperatively // Total elements = S*S // Threads per block = NSEQ_PER_BLOCK * S for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); // Pointer to observations for this sequence const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; // Load initial observation int obs0 = obs_seq[0]; float alpha_j = log_init[j] + log_B[j * num_obs + obs0]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { // store old alpha in shared s_log_alpha[threadIdx.x / S][j] = alpha_j; __syncthreads(); // Load observation if (j == 0) { s_obs[threadIdx.x / S] = obs_seq[t]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute logsumexp_i(old_alpha[i] + log_A[i][j]) float max_val = -INFINITY; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float candidate = s_log_alpha[threadIdx.x / S][i] + s_log_A[i * S + j]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, candidate); } float sum_exp = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_log_alpha[threadIdx.x / S][i] + s_log_A[i * S + j] - max_val); } float log_emit = log_B[j * num_obs + s_obs[threadIdx.x / S]]; alpha_j = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + log_emit; } // Final logsumexp over j s_log_alpha[threadIdx.x / S][j] = alpha_j; __syncthreads(); // Warp-level reduction? For log_B: if we transpose it, we have 16 contiguous loads per sequence per time step. That's a single memory transaction (if within a 64-byte cache line) or two. Since 16 floats = 64 bytes, and if contiguous, it's perfectly coalesced into one or two sectors. Excellent. For output: one float per sequence. Coalesced across blocks. So yes, we should transpose log_B on the Python side. Let's also think about whether we should normalize parameters in Python or in the kernel. The reference does _normalize_log, which is log-sum-exp normalization. For small S=16, it's cheap. But we can do it in Python with PyTorch, or in the kernel. Since we want to compare speed with reference, and normalization is done once per forward call (not per time step), doing it in Python is fine. But actually, it's three small operations. We can do them in Python and pass the normalized values to the kernel, or do them in the kernel. Since the Python overhead of three small ops is negligible, I'll do them in Python. Actually, wait: the reference calls _normalize_log on log_init, log_trans, log_emit before the loop. We can do the same in Python. Let me draft the code structure: ```python import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = """ #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> template <int S, int NSEQ_PER_BLOCK> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel( const int* __restrict__ observations, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T, int num_obs) { const int lane = threadIdx.x % S; const int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S; const int seq = blockIdx.x * NSEQ_PER_BLOCK + seq_local; if (seq >= B) return; // Shared memory __shared__ float s_log_A[S * S]; __shared__ float s_alpha[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK * S]; __shared__ int s_obs[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK]; // Load log_A cooperatively for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; // Initial state float alpha = log_init[lane] + log_B_t[obs_seq[0] * S + lane]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { // Store alpha in shared s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = alpha; __syncthreads(); // Load observation if (lane == 0) { s_obs[seq_local] = obs_seq[t]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute max over i float max_val = -1e20f; // avoid INFINITY macro issues #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float candidate = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, candidate); } // Compute sum of exp float sum_exp = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane] - max_val); } float emit = log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]; alpha = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + emit; } // Final reduction: logsumexp over lane (states) s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = alpha; __syncthreads(); // Reduction for max float max_val = alpha; if (lane < 8) max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 8]); s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = max_val; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 4) max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 4]); s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = max_val; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 2) max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 2]); s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = max_val; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 1) max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 1]); // Now max_val in lane 0 is the true max __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { s_alpha[seq_local * S] = max_val; // store max } __syncthreads(); float sum_exp = expf(alpha - s_alpha[seq_local * S]); // sum reduction if (lane < 8) sum_exp += s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 8]; s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = sum_exp; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 4) sum_exp += s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 4]; s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = sum_exp; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 2) sum_exp += s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 2]; s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane] = sum_exp; __syncthreads(); if (lane < 1) sum_exp += s_alpha[seq_local * S + lane + 1]; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = s_alpha[seq_local * S] + logf(sum_exp); } } torch::Tensor hmm_forward_cuda( torch::Tensor observations, torch::Tensor log_init, torch::Tensor log_A, torch::Tensor log_B_t) { // observations: (B, T) int32 // log_init: (S,) float32 // log_A: (S, S) float32 // log_B_t: (num_obs, S) float32 transposed int B = observations.size(0); int T = observations.size(1); int S = log_init.size(0); int num_obs = log_B_t.size(0); auto output = torch::empty({B}, log_init.options()); const int NSEQ_PER_BLOCK = 4; int threads = NSEQ_PER_BLOCK * S; // 64 int blocks = (B + NSEQ_PER_BLOCK - 1) / NSEQ_PER_BLOCK; // Ensure contiguous auto obs_int = observations.to(torch::kInt32).contiguous(); if (S == 16) { hmm_forward_kernel<16, 4><<<blocks, threads>>>( obs_int.data_ptr<int>(), log_init.data_ptr<float>(), log_A.data_ptr<float>(), log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, T, num_obs ); } else { // generic dispatch if needed, but for this problem S=16 AT_ERROR("Only S=16 supported for now"); } return output; } """ cpp_source = """ torch::Tensor hmm_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor observations, torch::Tensor log_init, torch::Tensor log_A, torch::Tensor log_B_t); """ hmm_cuda = load_inline(name="hmm_cuda", cpp_sources=cpp_source, cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=["hmm_forward_cuda"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"]) class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, num_states, num_obs): super().__init__() self.num_states = num_states self.num_obs = num_obs self.log_init = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states)) self.log_trans = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_states)) self.log_emit = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_obs)) def _normalize_log(self, x, dim=-1): return x - torch.logsumexp(x, dim=dim, keepdim=True) def forward(self, observations: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor: log_pi = self._normalize_log(self.log_init) log_A = self._normalize_log(self.log_trans, dim=-1) log_B = self._normalize_log(self.log_emit, dim=-1) # Transpose log_B for coalesced access log_B_t = log_B.t().contiguous() return hmm_cuda.hmm_forward_cuda(observations, log_pi, log_A, log_B_t) ``` Wait, I need to make sure the template dispatch is correct. Example: S=10, lane = threadIdx.x % 10. For seq_local=0, threadIdx.x=0..9. For seq_local=1, threadIdx.x=10..19. When we do `s_alpha[seq_local*S + lane + 5]` for lane<5: - For thread 0 (seq0, lane0): reads index 0*10 + 5 = 5. That's lane 5 of seq0. Good. - For thread 10 (seq1, lane0): reads index 1*10 + 5 = 15. That's lane 5 of seq1. Good. - For thread 30 (seq3, lane0): reads index 3*10 + 5 = 35. Good. But wait, for threadIdx.x=30, lane = 30%10 = 0. seq_local = 30/10 = 3. Access is s_alpha[3*10 + 0 + 5] = s_alpha[35]. ThreadIdx.x=31: lane=1, seq=3. Access s_alpha[36]. ThreadIdx.x=32 would be in next warp if blockDim>32. In a warp of 32 threads: 0..31. seq_locals and lanes are interleaved. The access `seq_local*S + lane + offset` is: index = (threadIdx.x / S) * S + (threadIdx.x % S) + offset = threadIdx.x - (threadIdx.x % S) + (threadIdx.x % S) + offset = threadIdx.x + offset? Wait, `seq_local * S + lane = (threadIdx.x / S) * S + threadIdx.x % S`. This is NOT equal to threadIdx.x in general! E.g., S=10, thread 15: 15/10=1, 15%10=5, index=10+5=15. Oh, it IS equal to threadIdx.x for threadIdx.x < blockDim.x? Let's check: For integer division and modulo: a = (a / S) * S + (a % S). Yes! This identity holds. So `seq_local * S + lane == threadIdx.x`. Wait, is that right? seq_local is `threadIdx.x / S`, lane is `threadIdx.x % S`. So `seq_local*S + lane = threadIdx.x`. Exactly! So `s_alpha[seq_local*S + lane] = s_alpha[threadIdx.x]`. Then `s_alpha[seq_local*S + lane + offset] = s_alpha[threadIdx.x + offset]`. This means the reduction uses threadIdx.x + offset, which is within the same sequence as long as `lane + offset < S`, i.e., `threadIdx.x % S + offset < S`. If this holds, then `threadIdx.x + offset` is the same sequence because `(threadIdx.x + offset) / S = threadIdx.x / S` if `threadIdx.x % S + offset < S`. When `lane < offset`, `lane + offset` might be >= S? In our reduction, we do `if (lane < offset)` where offset = S/2, 4, etc. For this to stay within the same sequence, we need `lane + offset < S` for all `lane < offset`, which means `offset - 1 + offset < S` => `2*offset - 1 < S` => `offset <= S/2`. We use offset = S/2, S/4, etc. For S being a power of 2, this is fine. But for S=10, offset=5, lane=4 => 9 < 10, fine. lane=0..4 => 5..9, all < 10. Good. But what about S=3, offset=2? lane=1 => 1+2=3 >= 3. That's a problem! The thread would read into the next sequence. So the reduction tree works only if `S` is a power of 2, or at least even and we are careful. For generic S, we need a generic reduction. We can use a simple loop over S to find max and sum, but that's O(S) per thread instead of O(log S). For S=16, O(S)=16 is fine since we only do it once at the end. The cost is negligible compared to T*S*S. So for generic S, I'll skip the tree reduction and just have each thread participate in a sequential reduction using shared memory or have one thread compute the final result. Better generic reduction: ```cpp __shared__ float s_max[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK]; __shared__ float s_sum[NSEQ_PER_BLOCK]; // Each thread stores its alpha s_alpha[threadIdx_local] = alpha; // threadIdx_local = seq_local*S + lane, but as identity = threadIdx.x if block size matches __syncthreads(); // Find max: each sequence has one designated thread (lane==0) if (lane == 0) { float m = s_alpha[seq_local*S]; for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) m = fmaxf(m, s_alpha[seq_local*S + i]); s_max[seq_local] = m; } __syncthreads(); // Compute sum of exp float sum_exp_local = expf(alpha - s_max[seq_local]); // reduce sum: again lane==0 if (lane == 0) { float s = 0; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) s += expf(s_alpha[seq_local*S + i] - s_max[seq_local]); s_sum[seq_local] = s; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = s_max[seq_local] + logf(s_sum[seq_local]); } ``` For S=16, this means lane==0 does a loop of 16 for max and 16 for sum. Since there are NSEQ_PER_BLOCK sequences, NSEQ_PER_BLOCK threads do this work. Others are idle. For S=16, NSEQ=4, that's 4 threads doing 32 operations each. Total work: 128 ops. Tree reduction would be fewer operations but similar total time because memory bandwidth is not the bottleneck. And this is much simpler and works for any S. But wait, there are 4 active threads and 60 idle threads in this phase. But since block size is 64, and the active threads are within 4 different warps? No, lane==0 threads are threadIdx.x = 0, 16, 32, 48. They are in 4 different warps (warp 0 has threads 0..31, so thread 0 and 16 are in warp 0; thread 32 and 48 are in warp 1). So in warp 0, threads 0 and 16 are active. They both execute the max loop, but other threads in the warp are idle. No divergence! They execute the same loop instructions. In fact, thread 0 operates on seq_local=0, thread 16 on seq_local=1. They both do: ```cpp float m = s_alpha[seq_local*S]; for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) ... ``` Since S is uniform, they execute the same instructions. The memory accesses are to different shared memory regions, but that is handled via predication. So no divergence. This is fine. For power-of-2 S, the tree reduction is slightly faster but the difference is tiny. Using the generic approach is cleaner and robust. Let me redesign the generic kernel: ```cpp template <int NSEQ_PER_BLOCK> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel( const int* __restrict__ observations, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T, int S, int num_obs) { const int lane = threadIdx.x % S; const int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S; const int seq = blockIdx.x * NSEQ_PER_BLOCK + seq_local; if (seq >= B) return; // Shared mem extern __shared__ float s_mem[]; float* s_log_A = s_mem; // size: S*S float* s_alpha = s_log_A + S * S; // size: blockDim.x int* s_obs = (int*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x); float* s_max = (float*)(s_obs + NSEQ_PER_BLOCK); float* s_sum = s_max + NSEQ_PER_BLOCK; // Alternatively, use fixed max sizes if S is bounded. // But to be clean, let's use extern. // Load log_A for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; float alpha = log_init[lane] + log_B_t[obs_seq[0] * S + lane]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) s_obs[seq_local] = obs_seq[t]; __syncthreads(); float max_val = -INFINITY; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float cand = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, cand); } float sum_exp = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane] - max_val); } alpha = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]; } // Final reduction s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { float max_val = s_alpha[seq_local * S]; for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) { max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + i]); } s_max[seq_local] = max_val; } __syncthreads(); float max_val = s_max[seq_local]; float sum_exp = 0.0f; // Compute sum of exp - we can have all threads participate and reduce, or one thread. // Let's have one thread for simplicity. if (lane == 0) { for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - max_val); } s_sum[seq_local] = sum_exp; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = max_val + logf(s_sum[seq_local]); } } ``` Wait, `extern __shared__` makes shared memory sizing dynamic. We need to pass the size in bytes during kernel launch: `<<<blocks, threads, shared_mem_bytes>>>`. shared_mem_bytes = S*S*sizeof(float) + blockDim.x*sizeof(float) + NSEQ_PER_BLOCK*sizeof(int) + 2*NSEQ_PER_BLOCK*sizeof(float). For S=16, blockDim.x = NSEQ_PER_BLOCK * S. Let's pick NSEQ_PER_BLOCK=4, blockDim.x=64. shared mem = 256*4 + 64*4 + 4*4 + 8*4 = 1024 + 256 + 16 + 32 = 1328 bytes. Very small. But wait, for generic S, we need to pick blockDim.x and NSEQ_PER_BLOCK. Since blockDim.x = NSEQ_PER_BLOCK * S, and we want blockDim.x to be a multiple of 32 (warp size) for good occupancy. Algorithm to pick threads per block: ```cpp int seq_per_block = 1; // Choose NSEQ_PER_BLOCK so that threads is a multiple of 32 and >= 64 while (seq_per_block * S < 64 && seq_per_block * S < 1024) { seq_per_block++; } if (seq_per_block * S > 1024) seq_per_block = 1024 / S; int threads = seq_per_block * S; if (threads == 0) threads = S; // S > 1024 (unlikely) if (threads % 32 != 0) { // round up to next multiple of 32, but ensure <= 1024 threads = ((threads + 31) / 32) * 32; if (threads > 1024) threads = (threads / 32 - 1) * 32; if (threads < S) threads = S; // but now threads/S may not be integer seq_per_block } // Actually, we must have threads % S == 0 for our mapping to work cleanly. // So find largest multiple of S that is <= 1024 and also a multiple of 32. int max_threads = 256; // target int threads = (max_threads / S) * S; if (threads == 0) threads = S; // Ensure multiple of 32 if (threads % 32 != 0) { // decrease to nearest multiple of 32 threads = (threads / 32) * 32; if (threads < S) threads = S; // may not be multiple of S anymore } ``` This is getting messy because threads must be multiple of S for the mapping. Dispatch to a templated version for specific S values: ```cpp #define DISPATCH_S(S_VAL) \ case S_VAL: { \ int seq_per_block = 256 / (S_VAL); \ if (seq_per_block < 1) seq_per_block = 1; \ int threads = seq_per_block * (S_VAL); \ int blocks = (B + seq_per_block - 1) / seq_per_block; \ size_t smem = (S_VAL)*(S_VAL)*sizeof(float) + threads*sizeof(float) + seq_per_block*sizeof(int) + 2*seq_per_block*sizeof(float); \ hmm_forward_kernel_template<(S_VAL)><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); \ break; \ } switch (S) { case 1: DISPATCH_S(1); break; case 2: DISPATCH_S(2); break; ... case 16: DISPATCH_S(16); break; ... default: TORCH_CHECK(false, "Unsupported num_states"); } ``` But with the template, the kernel signature doesn't have `S` parameter. So the templated kernel: ```cpp template <int S> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel_templated( const int* __restrict__ observations, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T, int num_obs) { const int seq_per_block = blockDim.x / S; const int lane = threadIdx.x % S; const int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S; const int seq = blockIdx.x * seq_per_block + seq_local; if (seq >= B) return; extern __shared__ float s_mem[]; float* s_log_A = s_mem; // S*S float* s_alpha = s_log_A + S * S; // blockDim.x int* s_obs = (int*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x); float* s_max = (float*)(s_obs + seq_per_block); float* s_sum = s_max + seq_per_block; // Load log_A for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; float alpha = log_init[lane] + log_B_t[obs_seq[0] * S + lane]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) s_obs[seq_local] = obs_seq[t]; __syncthreads(); float max_val = -INFINITY; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float cand = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, cand); } float sum_exp = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane] - max_val); } alpha = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]; } // Final reduction s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { float max_val = s_alpha[seq_local * S]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) { max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + i]); } s_max[seq_local] = max_val; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { float sum_exp = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - s_max[seq_local]); } s_sum[seq_local] = sum_exp; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = s_max[seq_local] + logf(s_sum[seq_local]); } } ``` This kernel uses S as template, so loops over S are unrolled. `seq_per_block` is dynamic. `blockDim.x` must be a multiple of S. For dispatch: ```cpp int seq_per_block = 256 / S; if (seq_per_block < 1) seq_per_block = 1; int threads = seq_per_block * S; if (threads > 1024) { // if S > 1024, adjust threads = (1024 / S) * S; if (threads == 0) threads = S; seq_per_block = threads / S; } int blocks = (B + seq_per_block - 1) / seq_per_block; size_t smem = S*S*sizeof(float) + threads*sizeof(float) + seq_per_block*sizeof(int) + 2*seq_per_block*sizeof(float); switch(S) { case 1: hmm_forward_kernel_templated<1><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); break; case 2: hmm_forward_kernel_templated<2><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); break; // ... up to 32 maybe case 16: hmm_forward_kernel_templated<16><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); break; case 32: hmm_forward_kernel_templated<32><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); break; case 64: hmm_forward_kernel_templated<64><<<blocks, threads, smem>>>(...); break; default: { // Fallback: non-template generic kernel or throw AT_ERROR("num_states=", S, " not in optimized dispatch list"); } } ``` But generating cases 1..64 is a macro. In the first loop ("find max"): ```cpp for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float cand = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, cand); } ``` At iteration i, s_alpha[seq_local*S + i] is broadcast within each sequence group. s_log_A[i*S + lane] is contiguous per sequence group. For warp 0: seq0 reads log_A[i*16 + 0..15], seq1 reads log_A[i*16 + 0..15]. Since the addresses are the same, no conflict. That's perfect! Same for the sum loop. Then log_B access: `log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]`. For fixed seq_local, lane varies. For warp 0: seq0 reads log_B_t[obs0 * 16 + 0..15], seq1 reads log_B_t[obs1 * 16 + 0..15]. If obs0 != obs1, these are different rows. But since the row size is 64 bytes (16 floats * 4), and each row starts at a multiple of 64 bytes. For seq0, addr = base + obs0*64 + lane*4. For seq1, addr = base + obs1*64 + lane*4. These accesses: for lane 0, addr0 = base + obs0*64, addr1 = base + obs1*64. In the same warp, threads 0 and 16 access two addresses separated by (obs1-obs0)*64. This is not coalesced across the warp: half the warp accesses one region, half accesses another. The GPU will issue two memory transactions (or more). But since the total is 32 floats = 128 bytes, and they are in at most two rows, it might be two transactions if obs0 and obs1 are different. Still very efficient. If obs0 == obs1, it's perfectly coalesced within the warp. Great. Now the final logsumexp: 1. Each thread stores alpha to shared. 2. `lane==0` reads all s_alpha[seq_local*S + i] for i=0..S-1 to find max. This is not broadcast, just sequential reads by one thread. Fine. 3. `lane==0` reads all again to compute sum of exp. Fine. Potential race condition? `s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads();` then `lane==0` reads. That's correct. But there's an issue with the reduction: `lane==0` in the same warp for different seq_locals: In warp 0, threads 0 and 16 are both lane==0 for their respective sequences. They both execute the reduction loop. They access: - thread 0: s_alpha[0..15] - thread 16: s_alpha[16..31] Different memory regions. No conflict. They both write to s_max[0] and s_max[1] respectively. Fine. Then all threads compute `expf(alpha - s_max[seq_local])`? Actually in my code above, the second phase is also done by lane==0 only. So after `__syncthreads()`, `lane==0` threads compute sum_exp and write to s_sum[seq_local]. Then `__syncthreads()`, then `lane==0` threads write output[seq]. Yes, that's fine. Wait, but after the first `__syncthreads()` before max reduction, all threads have written alpha. Then lane==0 computes max and writes to s_max. Then `__syncthreads()` to ensure s_max is visible. Then lane==0 computes sum_exp. That requires reading s_alpha again and s_max. Since s_max was just written by lane==0 threads, and we __syncthreads(), it's visible to all. But only lane==0 reads it. Then lane==0 writes s_sum. Another `__syncthreads()` to ensure s_sum visible. Then lane==0 reads s_sum and writes output. Actually, the second __syncthreads() is important because different lane==0 threads from different warps might finish at different times, and then if we write output before all s_sum are written, but since only lane==0 reads s_sum for its own seq_local, and each seq_local has exactly one lane==0 thread, there's no data race on s_sum between different seq_locals. But to be safe, __syncthreads() is cheap. Wait, I don't need the third __syncthreads() before writing output because: - Thread A (lane0, seq0) writes s_sum[0]. - Thread B (lane0, seq1) writes s_sum[1]. - They write to different addresses. No race. - Then thread A reads s_sum[0] and writes output[seq0]. - Thread B reads s_sum[1] and writes output[seq1]. - No race, no need for sync. But `__syncthreads()` is still needed before the final write if any other thread might read output? No, output is global. So I can remove the last __syncthreads(). Now, let me write the full Python code. ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline CUDA_SOURCE = r""" #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <math.h> template <int S> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel( const int* __restrict__ observations, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T, int num_obs) { const int seq_per_block = blockDim.x / S; const int lane = threadIdx.x % S; const int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S; const int seq = blockIdx.x * seq_per_block + seq_local; if (seq >= B) return; extern __shared__ float s_mem[]; float* s_log_A = s_mem; float* s_alpha = s_log_A + S * S; int* s_obs = (int*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x); float* s_max = (float*)(s_obs + seq_per_block); float* s_sum = s_max + seq_per_block; // Cooperative loading of log_A for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; // Initial alpha float alpha = log_init[lane] + log_B_t[obs_seq[0] * S + lane]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { // Write current alpha to shared for all threads in sequence to read s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); // Load next observation (one thread per sequence) if (lane == 0) { s_obs[seq_local] = obs_seq[t]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute max over previous states float max_val = -INFINITY; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float cand = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane]; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, cand); } // Compute sum of exp for logsumexp float sum_exp = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane] - max_val); } // Add emission and update alpha alpha = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]; } // Store final alpha s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); // Find max for final logsumexp if (lane == 0) { float max_val = s_alpha[seq_local * S]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) { max_val = fmaxf(max_val, s_alpha[seq_local * S + i]); } s_max[seq_local] = max_val; } __syncthreads(); // Compute sum of exp for final logsumexp if (lane == 0) { float sum_exp = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - s_max[seq_local]); } s_sum[seq_local] = sum_exp; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = s_max[seq_local] + logf(s_sum[seq_local]); } } // Generic fallback kernel without unrolling __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel_generic( const int* __restrict__ observations, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T, int S, int num_obs) { const int seq_per_block = blockDim.x / S; idx += blockDim.x) { s_log_A[idx] = log_A[idx]; } __syncthreads(); const int* obs_seq = observations + seq * T; float alpha = log_init[lane] + log_B_t[obs_seq[0] * S + lane]; for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha; max_val = fmaxf(max_val, cand); } float sum_exp = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_log_A[i * S + lane] - max_val); } alpha = max_val + logf(sum_exp) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + lane]; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { float sum_exp = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum_exp += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - s_max[seq_local]); } s_sum[seq_local] = sum_exp; } __syncthreads(); if (lane == 0) { output[seq] = s_max[seq_local] + logf(s_sum[seq_local]); } } torch::Tensor hmm_forward_cuda( torch::Tensor observations, torch::Tensor log_init, torch::Tensor log_A, torch::Tensor log_B_t) { int B = observations.size(0); int T = observations.size(1); int S = log_init.size(0); int num_obs = log_B_t.size(0); auto output = torch::empty({B}, log_init.options()); int seq_per_block = 256 / S; if (seq_per_block < 1) seq_per_block = 1; int threads = seq_per_block * S; if (threads > 1024) { threads = (1024 / S) * S; if (threads == 0) { threads = S; if (threads > 1024) { AT_ERROR("num_states too large: ", S); } } seq_per_block = threads / S; } int blocks = (B + seq_per_block - 1) / seq_per_block; size_t smem_size = S * S * sizeof(float) + threads * sizeof(float) + seq_per_block * sizeof(int) + 2 * seq_per_block * sizeof(float); switch (S) { case 1: hmm_forward_kernel<1><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>( observations.data_ptr<int>(), log_init.data_ptr<float>(), log_A.data_ptr<float>(), log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, T, num_obs ); break; case 2: hmm_forward_kernel<2><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>( observations.data_ptr<int>(), log_init.data_ptr<float>(), log_A.data_ptr<float>(), log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, T, num_obs ); For host side: ```cpp int seq_per_block = 256 / S; ... size_t smem_size = S * S * sizeof(float) + threads * sizeof(float) + seq_per_block * sizeof(int) + 2 * seq_per_block * sizeof(float); ``` This is valid host code. One more thing: I need to include `torch/extension.h` at the top of the CUDA source. This header includes pybind11 and ATen. The name "hmm_cuda" might conflict if not cleared. That's fine. One more thing: `observations.to(torch.int32)` - this creates a copy. For a tensor of size (64, 128), this is tiny. Negligible overhead. Now, let's think about the `_normalize_log` operations in PyTorch. They do: `x - torch.logsumexp(x, dim=..., keepdim=True)`. For `log_init` size 16: logsumexp over 16 elements. Very fast. For `log_A` size (16,16): logsumexp over dim=-1, 16 elements each. For `log_B` size (16,64): logsumexp over dim=-1, 64 elements each. These three operations plus transpose of log_B are negligible compared to the reference's T-loop. In our case, same. Potential issue: should we also fuse the normalization into the kernel? reasoning
The issue is that I'm using `long long` in the CUDA kernel but `data_ptr<long long>()` doesn't work with the PyTorch dispatch. The observations tensor is `torch.int64` / `torch.long`, so I need to use `int64_t` instead of `long long` for the data_ptr template. Let me fix that. Also, looking at the error, the issue was specifically with `data_ptr<long long>`. Let me use `int64_t` from `<stdint.h>` or `cstdint`.

So best practice in PyTorch C++ extensions: - For int32, use `int32_t` or `int` - For int64, use `int64_t` (which is `long` on Linux) - For long long, you're asking for trouble So my first attempt with `long long` was bad because I used `long long` explicitly. Within a warp, for logsumexp: - Each thread computes `val = alpha[i] + A[i][lane]` for all i, finding local max - Then need to reduce max across the 16 threads in the same sequence. - With warp shuffle, thread in lane j can get values from other lanes in same sequence. But since a sequence's lanes are `lane = threadIdx.x % 16`, they are not at uniform intervals in the warp. For threadIdx.x, the sequence group is `threadIdx.x / 16`. In a warp of 32, there are 2 sequences: one with threadIdx.x in {0..15}, another in {16..31}. For shuffle within a sequence: lanes 0..15 and 16..31. But `__shfl_sync` operates on lane IDs within the warp. So sequence 0 threads can use lanes 0..15. Sequence 1 threads can use lanes 16..31. If I want to reduce max across lanes 0..15: ```cpp float max_val = local_max; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 8; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, max_val, offset); max_val = fmaxf(max_val, other); } ``` But this would shuffle across the full warp, mixing sequence 0 and sequence 1! Because `__shfl_down_sync` with offset 8 on lane 8 gets lane 16, which is sequence 1! To avoid this, I need a custom mask or offset calculation. I can use: ```cpp int warp_lane = threadIdx.x & 31; int seq_in_warp = warp_lane / 16; // 0 or 1 int lane_in_seq = warp_lane % 16; ... for (int offset = 8; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { int src_lane = warp_lane + offset; // But this might read from the other sequence. } ``` Actually, it's simpler to just NOT use warp shuffles and instead have each thread independently read all alpha[i] from shared memory. Given S=16, this is only 16 reads per thread, which is trivial. The shared memory access pattern has no bank conflicts as I analyzed. So I'll stick with the shared-memory approach. Let me write a clean, optimized kernel: ```cuda template <int S> __global__ void hmm_forward_kernel( const int32_t* __restrict__ obs, const float* __restrict__ log_init, const float* __restrict__ log_A, const float* __restrict__ log_B_t, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int T) { const int seq = blockIdx.x * (blockDim.x / S) + (threadIdx.x / S); const int s = threadIdx.x % S; if (seq >= B) return; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* s_A = smem; // S * S int32_t* s_obs = (int32_t*)(s_A + S * S); // seq_per_block float* s_temp = (float*)(s_obs + ((blockDim.x / S + 1) & ~1)); // blockDim.x for alpha // Load transition matrix to shared memory #pragma unroll for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) { s_A[i] = log_A[i]; } __syncthreads(); const int32_t* my_obs = obs + seq * T; float alpha = log_init[s] + log_B_t[my_obs[0] * S + s]; #pragma unroll 4 for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) { s_temp[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (s == 0) { s_obs[threadIdx.x / S] = my_obs[t]; } __syncthreads(); float m = -1e20f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { float val = s_temp[(threadIdx.x / S) * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s]; m = fmaxf(m, val); } float sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum += expf(s_temp[(threadIdx.x / S) * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s] - m); } alpha = m + logf(sum) + log_B_t[s_obs[threadIdx.x / S] * S + s]; } s_temp[threadIdx.x] = alpha; __syncthreads(); if (s == 0) { float m = s_temp[(threadIdx.x / S) * S]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) { m = fmaxf(m, s_temp[(threadIdx.x / S) * S + i]); } float sum = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) { sum += expf(s_temp[(threadIdx.x / S) * S + i] - m); } output[seq] = m + logf(sum); } } ``` For S=16, blockDim.x = 128 gives 8 sequences per block. Shared memory: 16*16*4 + 8*4 + 128*4 = 1024 + 32 + 512 = 1568 bytes. Very small. I should use `-O3` and maybe `--use_fast_math` for faster log/exp. But `--use_fast_math` might reduce precision. Let me write a very clean, well-optimized CUDA kernel for S=16. Given S=16, I'll use `blockDim.x = 256` which gives 16 sequences per block. Shared memory: - log_A: 16 * 16 * 4 = 1024 bytes - alpha values: 256 * 4 = 1024 bytes - obs: 16 * 4 = 64 bytes - max/sum: 16 * 4 * 2 = 128 bytes Total: ~3200 bytes Occupancy: With 3200 bytes shared memory per block, and 48KB per SM, we can run 15 blocks per SM. With B=64 and 16 seqs per block, we have 4 blocks total. That's not enough to saturate the GPU, but the algorithm is sequential per sequence anyway, so latency hiding is limited. Actually, let's use fewer threads per block to launch more blocks. With S=16, if we use 64 threads per block (4 sequences per block), we get 16 blocks for B=64. That might be better for occupancy. Each block: 64 threads Shared memory: 1024 + 256 + 16 + 128 = ~1424 bytes 16 blocks across the GPU - this gives better parallelism but still limited. The kernel is memory-bound with a lot of exp/log per step. But since everything is in shared memory and registers, it should be compute-bound on exp/log. For each timestep per sequence: - 16 reads from alpha (shared mem) - 16 reads from A (shared mem) - 16 fmaxf - 16 expf - 16 reads again - 1 logf - 1 read from log_B_t (global mem) The global mem read for log_B_t is only 1 per thread per timestep, so very little bandwidth. Actually, log_B_t is in global memory. For 64 sequences * 128 timesteps * 16 states = 131072 reads from log_B_t. That's ~512 KB of memory traffic. Negligible. So this should be very fast. Let me also consider using `__expf` (fast exp) and `__logf` (fast log). These have lower precision but are much faster. With 1e-4 tolerance, they should be okay, especially since the reference uses PyTorch's logsumexp which might also not be perfectly precise. But I'll use standard `expf` and `logf` for safety. Actually, the bottleneck is sequential execution across T timesteps with many syncs. We can't parallelize across T because of the dependency chain. But we can overlap multiple sequences. For 16 blocks * 64 threads each running 128 timesteps, the GPU is doing 128*4 = 512 sequential iterations per block. With 16 blocks, that's 8192 sequential time-steps to work through, which should keep the GPU busy enough given the computation per step. I think this kernel will easily beat the reference. For `log_B`, I'll transpose it to `log_B_t` so that `log_B_t[obs * S + s]` is coalesced. Since each thread in a warp reads `log_B_t[obs * S + s]` with different `s`, and obs is the same for all threads in the sequence, the access pattern is: - Thread s=0 reads log_B_t[obs*S + 0] - Thread s=1 reads log_B_t[obs*S + 1] - ... These are consecutive floats in memory, so coalesced! Perfect. For the final reduction over alpha to compute output[seq], I'll have thread s=0 do a simple loop over the 16 alpha values stored in shared memory. Let me finalize the code. I'll use the name `hmm_forward_cuda` and make sure to include the right headers. ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <math.h> #include <stdint.h> ``` One tricky thing: `extern __shared__ float s_mem[];` means dynamic shared memory. The size must be specified at kernel launch. The compiler pads arrays for alignment. I'll be careful with the layout. Actually, to avoid alignment issues with int32_t, I'll use separate shared memory arrays if possible, but with `extern __shared__` we get one array. I'll calculate offsets carefully: ```cpp extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* s_A = smem; // S*S floats float* s_alpha = s_A + S * S; // blockDim.x floats int32_t* s_obs = (int32_t*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x); // seq_per_block int32s float* s_max = (float*)(s_obs + ((seq_per_block + 1) & ~1)); // seq_per_block floats, aligned float* s_sum = s_max + seq_per_block; // seq_per_block floats ``` The alignment for `s_obs` after `s_alpha` is fine because `s_alpha + blockDim.x` is float-aligned, and `int32_t` has the same alignment requirement as float (4 bytes). For `s_max` after `s_obs`, I ensure `s_obs` has an even number of elements so the total bytes are a multiple of 8, ensuring `s_max` is 4-byte aligned (which it naturally would be anyway). Actually, I think this alignment is fine for the small sizes. Let me keep it simple but safe. import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

CUDA_SOURCE = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <math.h>

template <int S>
__global__ void hmm_forward_kernel_const(
    const int64_t* __restrict__ observations,
    const float* __restrict__ log_init,
    const float* __restrict__ log_A,
    const float* __restrict__ log_B_t,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int B, int T, int num_obs)
{
    int seq_per_block = blockDim.x / S;
    int s = threadIdx.x % S;
    int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S;
    int seq = blockIdx.x * seq_per_block + seq_local;

    if (seq >= B) return;

    extern __shared__ float smem[];
    float* s_A = smem;
    float* s_alpha = s_A + S * S;
    int64_t* s_obs = (int64_t*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x);

    for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) {
        s_A[i] = log_A[i];
    }
    __syncthreads();

    const int64_t* my_obs = observations + seq * T;
    float alpha = log_init[s] + log_B_t[my_obs[0] * S + s];

    for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) {
        s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha;
        __syncthreads();

        if (s == 0) {
            s_obs[seq_local] = my_obs[t];
        }
        __syncthreads();

        float m = -1e30f;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            float val = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s];
            m = fmaxf(m, val);
        }

        float sum = 0.0f;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            sum += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s] - m);
        }

        alpha = m + logf(sum) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + s];
    }

    s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha;
    __syncthreads();

    if (s == 0) {
        float m = s_alpha[seq_local * S];
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) {
            m = fmaxf(m, s_alpha[seq_local * S + i]);
        }
        float sum = 0.0f;
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            sum += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - m);
        }
        output[seq] = m + logf(sum);
    }
}

__global__ void hmm_forward_kernel_generic(
    const int64_t* __restrict__ observations,
    const float* __restrict__ log_init,
    const float* __restrict__ log_A,
    const float* __restrict__ log_B_t,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int B, int T, int S, int num_obs)
{
    int seq_per_block = blockDim.x / S;
    int s = threadIdx.x % S;
    int seq_local = threadIdx.x / S;
    int seq = blockIdx.x * seq_per_block + seq_local;

    if (seq >= B) return;

    extern __shared__ float smem[];
    float* s_A = smem;
    float* s_alpha = s_A + S * S;
    int64_t* s_obs = (int64_t*)(s_alpha + blockDim.x);

    for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) {
        s_A[i] = log_A[i];
    }
    __syncthreads();

    const int64_t* my_obs = observations + seq * T;
    float alpha = log_init[s] + log_B_t[my_obs[0] * S + s];

    for (int t = 1; t < T; ++t) {
        s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha;
        __syncthreads();

        if (s == 0) {
            s_obs[seq_local] = my_obs[t];
        }
        __syncthreads();

        float m = -1e30f;
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            float val = s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s];
            m = fmaxf(m, val);
        }

        float sum = 0.0f;
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            sum += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] + s_A[i * S + s] - m);
        }

        alpha = m + logf(sum) + log_B_t[s_obs[seq_local] * S + s];
    }

    s_alpha[threadIdx.x] = alpha;
    __syncthreads();

    if (s == 0) {
        float m = s_alpha[seq_local * S];
        for (int i = 1; i < S; ++i) {
            m = fmaxf(m, s_alpha[seq_local * S + i]);
        }
        float sum = 0.0f;
        for (int i = 0; i < S; ++i) {
            sum += expf(s_alpha[seq_local * S + i] - m);
        }
        output[seq] = m + logf(sum);
    }
}

torch::Tensor hmm_forward_cuda(
    torch::Tensor observations,
    torch::Tensor log_init,
    torch::Tensor log_A,
    torch::Tensor log_B_t)
{
    int B = observations.size(0);
    int T = observations.size(1);
    int S = log_init.size(0);
    int num_obs = log_B_t.size(0);

    auto output = torch::empty({B}, log_init.options());

    int seq_per_block = 256 / S;
    if (seq_per_block < 1) seq_per_block = 1;
    int threads = seq_per_block * S;
    if (threads > 1024) {
        threads = (1024 / S) * S;
        if (threads == 0) threads = S;
        seq_per_block = threads / S;
    }
    int blocks = (B + seq_per_block - 1) / seq_per_block;

    size_t smem_size = S * S * sizeof(float)
                     + threads * sizeof(float)
                     + seq_per_block * sizeof(int64_t);

    if (observations.dtype() != torch::kInt64) {
        observations = observations.to(torch::kInt64);
    }

    switch (S) {
        case 1:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<1><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 2:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<2><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 4:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<4><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 8:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<8><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 16:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<16><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 32:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<32><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        case 64:
            hmm_forward_kernel_const<64><<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, num_obs
            ); break;
        default:
            hmm_forward_kernel_generic<<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>(
                observations.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
                log_init.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_A.data_ptr<float>(),
                log_B_t.data_ptr<float>(),
                output.data_ptr<float>(),
                B, T, S, num_obs
            ); break;
    }

    return output;
}

CPP_SOURCE = r"""
torch::Tensor hmm_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor observations, torch::Tensor log_init, torch::Tensor log_A, torch::Tensor log_B_t);
"""

hmm_cuda = load_inline(
    name="hmm_cuda_final",
    cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCE,
    cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,
    functions=["hmm_forward_cuda"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
    verbose=False,
)


class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, num_states, num_obs):
        super().__init__()
        self.num_states = num_states
        self.num_obs = num_obs
        self.log_init = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states))
        self.log_trans = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_states))
        self.log_emit = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_states, num_obs))

    def _normalize_log(self, x, dim=-1):
        return x - torch.logsumexp(x, dim=dim, keepdim=True)

    def forward(self, observations: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        B, T = observations.shape
        log_pi = self._normalize_log(self.log_init)
        log_A = self._normalize_log(self.log_trans, dim=-1)
        log_B = self._normalize_log(self.log_emit, dim=-1)

        log_B_t = log_B.t().contiguous()
        obs = observations.to(device=self.log_init.device).contiguous()
        log_pi_c = log_pi.contiguous()
        log_A_c = log_A.contiguous()

        return hmm_cuda.hmm_forward_cuda(obs, log_pi_c, log_A_c, log_B_t)
